<A NAME="_Toc305669983"></A><P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>INTRODUCTION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. is organized under the laws of British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;In this Annual Report, the &#147;Company&#148;, &#147;Barrier&#148;, &#147;we&#148;, &#147;our&#148; and &#147;us&#148; refer to International Barrier Technology Inc. and its subsidiaries (unless the context otherwise requires). &nbsp;We refer you to the actual corporate documents for more complete information than may be contained in this Annual Report. &nbsp;Our principal corporate offices are located at 510 4th Street North, Watkins, Minnesota, USA &nbsp;55389. &nbsp;Our telephone number is 320-764-5797.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>BUSINESS OF INTERNATIONAL BARRIER TECHNOLOGY INC.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. develops, manufactures, and markets proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire. &nbsp;The Company uses a patented, non-combustible, non-toxic <I>Pyrotite&#174;</I> formulation that is used to coat wood panels and has potential application to engineered wood products, paint, plastics, and expanded polystyrene. &nbsp;Sales have been US$4.1 million and US$3.3 million during Fiscal 2012 and 2011, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>FINANCIAL AND OTHER INFORMATION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>In this Annual Report, unless otherwise specified, all dollar amounts are expressed in U.S. Dollars (&#147;$&#148;).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:24pt; margin-top:6.667px; margin-bottom:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B>ITEM 1. &nbsp;BUSINESS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>1.A. &nbsp;General Development of Business</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><U>Introduction</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. and its subsidiaries are collectively hereinafter referred to as the &#147;Company&#148;.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Incorporated in July 1986, pursuant to agreements, the Company acquired the rights to the Pyrotite Technology for Canada in July 1986 and for the United States in March 1992. &nbsp;The Canadian rights and the US rights under the 1992 agreement were voluntarily terminated in January 1996 due to marketing conflict with a corporation which acquired the licensor&#146;s rights to the technology. &nbsp;A new agreement for the rights in the United States was signed in January 1996 and revised in March 1996. &nbsp;The Company acquired the world-wide rights to the Pyrotite technology, including: US patents; foreign patent filings; manufacturing know-how; trade secrets, and trademarks pursuant to a March 2004 agreement. &nbsp;The Company completed construction of a new manufacturing facility in Minnesota, USA in December 1995; the facility was upgraded to include substantial automation, increased capacity and product quality in April/May 2000; as Barrier continued to achieve double digit growth year after year, it decided the current manufacturing facility needed to be expanded. &nbsp;The planning and development of a higher volume and more fully automated facility began in 2004; the first phase that included the building addition was complete in March 2005. &nbsp;The second phase of the new line development was complete in August 2005 and the first commercial production run was in March 2006. &nbsp;The final phase of equipment installation, shake down improvements, and training was complete in late 2006 at which time full commercial production began.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company has been involved in the development and manufacturing/marketing of fire-rated building products since 1986, including current products: Pyrotite, a fire-barrier material comprised of the patented formulation reinforced with chopped fiberglass strands and applied adhered directly to structural sheathing (OSB &#150; oriented strand board or plywood) designed to prevent ignition and inhibit the spread of flames. &nbsp;The products are currently marketed through exclusive supply agreements as LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; Fire-Rated OSB Sheathing into Residential Roof Deck, Wall Assembly, Wildland Urban Interface Zones, and Structurally Insulated Panel market; and MuleHide FR Deck Panel into the commercial modular market. &nbsp;On January 18, 2011, LP and Barrier extended their existing Supply Agreement through December 31, 2013. LP is the largest producer of Oriented Strand Board (OSB) in the world and believes that Barrier&#146;s Pyrotite&#174; Technology will help them achieve their strategy of providing a number of value added OSB products to the building community. The agreement gives LP the exclusive right to sell Pyrotite&#174; treated panel products in North America, in all markets other than commercial modular (MuleHide Products, Inc.), under their brand name LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; Fire-Rated OSB Sheathing. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>1.C. &nbsp;Narrative Description of Business</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. (Barrier) manufactures and sells fire-rated building materials primarily in the United States. &nbsp;Barrier has a patented fire protective material (Pyrotite<font style='font-family:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman'>&#8482;</font>) that is applied to building materials to greatly improve their respective fire resistant properties. Coated wood panel products are sold to builders through building product distribution companies all over the United States. &nbsp;Many of the top multifamily homebuilders in the US utilize Barrier<font style='font-family:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman'>&#8217;</font>s fire-rated structural panel manufactured with Pyrotite<font style='font-family:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman'>&#8482;</font> in areas where the building code requires the use of a fire-rated building panel.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier sells LP&#174; FlameBlock Fire-Rated OSB Sheathing to LP&#174; Building Products and sales to LP accounted for 61% of Fiscal 2012 revenues. &nbsp;Barrier sells MuleHide FR Deck Panel to MuleHide Products, Inc. and sales to MuleHide accounted for 38% of Fiscal 2012 revenues. &nbsp;In 2011, sales to LP accounted for 26% of sales revenues and MuleHide accounted for 72%. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>5</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Seasonality</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The building products industry in the United States does experience seasonality with housing starts generally depressed in winter months. &nbsp;Barrier<font style='font-family:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman'>&#8217;</font>s Pyrotite<font style='font-family:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman'>&#8482;</font> products, however, is sold in housing markets that have excellent winter business, including the states of Florida and California. &nbsp;Also, much of the modular housing, including the foam core panel market, performs a considerable amount of their required construction inside factories. Since the work is done within protected environments they tend to be less impacted by the winter season than typical building projects. &nbsp;Seasonality, therefore, is not considered to be a major impediment to Barrier&#146;s success in the US market place.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Dependency upon Patents/Licenses/Processes</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Pursuant to an agreement for sale of technology dated 3/1/2004 (&#147;original agreement&#148;), between the Company and Pyrotite Corporation, the Company acquired the rights (previously licensed) to certain fire retardant technology and trademarks for $1,000,000. &nbsp;These rights and technology included all of the patents that deal with &#147;surface applied&#148; Pyrotite technology. The agreement further acknowledged that Pyrotite Corporation retained ownership of &#147;integral&#148; OSB technology (IPOSB) but the parties agreed that Pyrotite would share revenues with the Company for: gross sales of any IPOSB products or substances manufactured in or sold into the US, by or on the behalf of, Pyrotite Corporation; or, for certain rights or license fees received by Pyrotite Corporation for use of the technology.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>A dispute ensued between the parties as to the correct amounts owed to the Company by Pyrotite pursuant to the revenue sharing clause of the original agreement. &nbsp;As a result, the parties, through a mediator, reached a settlement on March 23, 2010 whereby Pyrotite agreed to pay the Company $90,000 in full settlement of prior amounts in dispute. &nbsp;In addition, Pyrotite agreed to convey all of its right, title and interest in IPOSB technology to the Company. There was no value attributed to the IPOSB technology in the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier utilizes patented manufacturing technology, as well as manufacturing know-how and trade secrets that have been developed and are closely protected by Barrier.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The manufacturing process for the Pyrotite&#174; products is protected by trade secrets and patent pending status on an improved technology. &nbsp;International Barrier Technology, Inc. and Barrier Technology Corporation are, in that regard, totally dependent upon these for success in the business.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>All employees are required to sign a Confidentiality Agreement that incorporates a &#147;do not compete clause&#148;. &nbsp;As these clauses pertain to Barrier&#146;s employees at the US operations, they have been drafted to conform to the strictest interpretation under Minnesota law.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Employees</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>As of 8/31/2012, the Company had 16 full-time employees, one full time Executive Officer and two part-time Executive Officers. &nbsp;As of 6/30/2012, the Company had 15 full-time employees, one full-time Executive Officer and two part-time Executive Officers. As of 6/30/2011, the Company had 15 full-time employees, one full-time Executive Officer and two part-time Executive Officers.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Dependency upon Customers</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><U>Fiscal 2012</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>During Fiscal 2012, the company&#146;s largest customer was LP&#174; Building Products (LP). &nbsp;LP is a partner that services the multifamily residential roof deck construction, wall assemblies, and structural insulated panels (SIPs)markets. &nbsp;LP purchased 65% of the 9,687,029 sq. ft. of Pyrotite&#174; products shipped in Fiscal 2012. &nbsp;LP is the largest producer of Oriented Strand Board (OSB) in the world and believes that Barrier&#146;s Pyrotite&#174; Technology will help them achieve their strategy of providing a number of value added OSB products to the building community. &nbsp;Through an exclusive supply agreement, LP has the exclusive right to sell Pyrotite&#174; treated panel products in North America, in all markets other </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>6</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>than the commercial modular (MuleHide Products, Inc.) market, under their brand name LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; Fire-Rated OSB Sheathing.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; is sold through wholesale distribution companies such as ProBuild, Builders FirstSource, Biewer Lumber, Weekes Forest Products (Logan Lumber), Taiga Building Products, Vandermeer Forest Products, Boise, Curtis Lumber, and Universal Forest Products. &nbsp;The Western Region market (CA-WA) was the strongest region in these markets with 32% of total sales into these markets. &nbsp;Other regions in these markets include the South, the Midwest, the MidAtlantic and Canada). &nbsp;The building products distribution companies mentioned have a presence in all of these areas and are consistent FlameBlock customers throughout these geographies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The second largest market for Pyrotite&#174; products was the commercial modular market. &nbsp;MuleHide Products, Inc. &#147;Mulehide&#148;. &nbsp;Mulehide is the company that services the commercial modular market including selling Pyrotite&#174; products to the commercial modular market. &nbsp;Commercial modular sales accounted for 35% of total shipments in 2012. &nbsp;Product shipped to MuleHide Products is through an exclusive supply agreement and private labeled MuleHide FR Deck Panel. &nbsp;The FR Deck Panel is distributed through ABC Supply Company locations throughout the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><U>Fiscal 2011</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>During Fiscal 2011, the company&#146;s largest customer was MuleHide Products, Inc. &#147;Mulehide&#148;. &nbsp;Mulehide is a company that services the commercial roofing market including selling Pyrotite&#174; products to the commercial modular roof deck market. &nbsp;MuleHide purchased 56% of the 6,962,264 sq. ft. of Pyrotite&#174; products shipped in Fiscal 2011. &nbsp;Product shipped to MuleHide Products is through an exclusive supply agreement and private labeled MuleHide FR Deck Panel. The FR Deck Panel is distributed through ABC Supply Company locations throughout the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The largest market for Pyrotite&#174; products (after accounting for FR Deck Panel) in Fiscal 2011 remained roof deck applications in multifamily residential roof deck construction, wall assemblies and structural insulated panels (SIPs). &nbsp;On January 18, 2011, LP and Barrier extended their existing Supply Agreement through December 31, 2013. &nbsp;LP is the largest producer of Oriented Strand Board (OSB) in the world and believes that Barrier&#146;s Pyrotite&#174; Technology will help them achieve their strategy of providing a number of value added OSB products to the building community. &nbsp;The agreement gives LP the exclusive right to sell Pyrotite&#174; treated panel products in North America, in all markets other than the commercial modular (MuleHide Products, Inc.), under their brand name LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; Fire-Rated OSB Sheathing. &nbsp;Barrier will provide technical support. Barrier will continue to supply MuleHide FR panel to MuleHide Products, Inc. under the existing Supply Agreement executed between Barrier and MuleHide in 2004.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Multifamily residential roof deck, wall assembly, and structural insulated panel markets accounted for 44% of total shipments in 2011. &nbsp;Sales into these markets are now made as LP&#174; FlameBlock&#174; through LP&#174; Building Products and wholesale distribution companies such as ProBuild, BFS Building Supply, Biewer Lumber, Logan Lumber Company, Taiga Building Products, Vandermeer Forest Products, Boise, Curtis Lumber, and Universal Forest Products. &nbsp;The Western Region market (CA-WA) was the strongest region in these markets with 28.5% of total sales into these markets. &nbsp;Other regions in these markets include Florida, the Midwest, and the MidAtlantic). &nbsp;The building products distribution companies mentioned have a presence in all of these areas and are consistent FlameBlock customers throughout these geographies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>1.D. &nbsp;Financial Information About Geographic Areas</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman">During Fiscal 2012 and 2011, all sales were in the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>At 6/30/2012 and 6/30/2011: $3,583,555 and $3,688,347 of the assets were located in the United States and $124,490 and $313,888 were located in Canada, respectively.</P>

<A NAME="_Toc305669985"></A><P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>ITEM 1A. &nbsp;RISK FACTORS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>In addition to the other information presented in this Annual Report, the following should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company and its business. &nbsp;This Annual Report contains forward-looking statements that involve risks and uncertainties. &nbsp;The Company's actual results may differ materially from results discussed in the forward-looking statements. &nbsp;Factors that might cause such a difference include those discussed below and elsewhere in this Annual Report.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>General Corporate Risks</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Investors may be disadvantaged because the Company is incorporated in Canada, which has different laws.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The articles/by-laws and the laws of Canada are different from those typical in the United States. &nbsp;The typical rights of investors in Canadian companies differ modestly from those in the United States. &nbsp;Such differences may cause investors legal difficulties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>U.S. investors may not be able to enforce their civil liabilities against the Company or its directors, controlling persons and officers.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>It may be difficult to bring and enforce suits against the Company. &nbsp;The Company is a corporation incorporated under the laws of the British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;A majority of the Company's directors are resident outside the United States, and all or substantial portions of their assets are located outside of the United States. &nbsp;As a result, it may be difficult for U.S. holders of the Company&#146;s common shares to effect service of process on these persons within the United States or to realize in the United States upon judgments rendered against them. &nbsp;In addition, a shareholder should not assume that the courts of Canada (i) would enforce judgments of U.S. courts obtained in actions against the Company or such persons predicated upon the civil liability provisions of the U.S. federal securities laws or other laws of the United States, or (ii) would enforce, in original actions, liabilities against us or such persons predicated upon the U.S. federal securities laws or other laws of the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Passive Foreign Investment Company (&#147;PFIC&#148;) designation could lead to an adverse tax situation for U.S. investors.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>U.S. investors in the Company could be subject to U.S. taxation at possibly adverse or higher rates and under a system that might be more complicated and unfamiliar to them. &nbsp;For example, a U.S investor might be subject to special tax rules with respect to any &#147;excess distribution&#148; received and any gain realized from a sale or other disposition (including a pledge) of that holder's shares. &nbsp;Distributions a U.S. investor receives in a taxable year that are greater than 125% of the average annual distributions received during the shorter of the three preceding taxable years or the holder's holding period for the shares will be treated as excess distributions. &nbsp;For example, under certain circumstances, a U.S. investor who is an individual might be subject to information reporting requirements and backup withholding, currently at a 28% rate, on dividends received on common shares. &nbsp;If a U.S. Holder holds shares in any year in which the Company is a PFIC, that holder might be required to file Internal Revenue Service Form 8621.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>Risks Relating to Financial Condition</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>The Company has accumulated losses since inception.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Since inception through June 30, 2012, the Company has incurred aggregate losses of ($14,730,354). &nbsp;Our earnings (losses) from operations for years ended 6/30/2012 and 6/30/2011 were ($139,696) and $895,811, respectively; our cash used in operations for years ended 6/30/2012 and 6/30/2011 was $244,349 and $329,065, respectively. &nbsp;These factors cast substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. &nbsp;There is no assurance that we will operate profitably or will generate positive cash flow in the future. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s financial statements have been prepared on a going concern basis, </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>8</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>which assumes the Company will be able to realize its assets and discharge its obligations and commitments in the normal course of operations. &nbsp;Realization values maybe substantially different from carrying values and classification of assets and liabilities should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern. &nbsp;In addition, our operating results in the future may be subject to significant fluctuations due to many factors not within our control, such as the unpredictability of when customers will order products, the size of customers' orders, the demand for our products, the level of competition or general economic conditions. Consequently, the Company expects to incur operating losses and negative cash flow until our products gain market acceptance sufficient to generate a commercially viable and sustainable level of sales, and/or additional products are developed and commercially released and sales of such products made so that we are operating in a profitable manner.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>The Company&#146;s history of operating losses is likely to lead to the need for additional, potentially unavailable, financings and related problems.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company has a history of losses: ($139,696) in FY2012 and $895,811 [&#147;profit&#148; result of non-cash flow &#147;change in fair value of derivative liability] in FY2011. &nbsp;Despite recent capital infusions, the Company will require significant additional funding to meet its long-term business objectives, unless the trend of losses is reversed. &nbsp;Capital will be needed to help maintain and to expand marketing of the Company&#146;s products. &nbsp;The Company may not be able to obtain additional financing on reasonable terms, or at all. &nbsp;If equity financing is required, then such financings could result in significant dilution to existing shareholders. &nbsp;If the Company is unable to obtain sufficient financing, the Company might have to dramatically slow marketing efforts and/or lose control of its products. &nbsp;The Company has historically obtained the preponderance of its financing through the issuance of equity. &nbsp;There is a limit of 100,000,000 authorized common shares. &nbsp;The Company has no current plans to obtain financing through means other than equity financing and/or loans. &nbsp;Such losses and the resulting need for external financings could result in losses of investment value.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>The Company&#146;s need for additional financing to expand production and conduct marketing efforts could lead to the Company&#146;s inability to continue generating material sales revenue.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company develops, manufactures, and markets proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire. Additional amounts of financing may be required to facilitate corporate operational growth and to expand marketing efforts on a short-term basis. &nbsp;Conventional bank financing was originally established at a local bank for up to $1,000,000 in the form of a revolving line of credit. In July 2008, the terms of the existing revolving bank facility of $1,000,000 were modified to be comprised of a $500,000 capital loan being amortized by the bank over a 10-year period and which is secured by building, property and equipment and a $500,000 credit facility as an operating line of credit at 7.5%. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In August 2010, the line of credit was amended to include a reduced limit of $250,000, and was extended until September 1, 2011 at a reduced interest rate of 6.75%. &nbsp;In December 2011, Barrier negotiated a term bank loan facility in the amount of $450,000 bearing interest at 6.25% and collateralized by a security interest in inventory, accounts receivable, equipment and all intangibles of the Company as well as an assignment of the building lease. The facility is being amortized over 4 years with fixed monthly blended payments of principal and interest totaling $6,800 with a balloon payment due on January 1, 2016. &nbsp;At June 30, 2012, the capital loan balance was $427,880. &nbsp;By a promissory note agreement dated December 29, 2011, the Company has arranged for credit facilities with Farmers State Bank of Watkins which allows the Company to be advanced up to $50,000 under the terms of the promissory note agreement. Advances will bear interest at 6.25% per annum and will be repayable in installments of accrued interest beginning February 1, 2012 with the entire unpaid Principal and interest to be repaid on February 1, 2013. &nbsp;Advances are collateralized by a security interest on inventory, accounts receivable, equipment and all intangibles of the Company as well as an assignment of the building lease.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>The Company competes with other building materials companies that have similar operations, and many such competitor companies have operations and financial resources and industry experience far greater than those of the Company.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>9</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Even if the Company maintains a successful marketing program, the Company will still be subject to competition from much larger and financially stronger competitors and such competition may materially adversely affect the Company&#146;s financial performance. &nbsp;Also, the Company&#146;s need to acquire inventory will require additional financial resources.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>Risks Relating to Management and Specific Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws contain provisions indemnifying its officers and directors against all costs, charges and expenses incurred by them.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws contain provisions that state, subject to applicable law, the Company shall indemnify every director or officer of the Company, subject to the limitations of the British Columbia Corporations Act, against all losses or liabilities that the Company&#146;s director or officer may sustain or incur in the execution of their duties. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws further state that no director of officer shall be liable for any loss, damage or misfortune that may happen to, or be incurred by the Company in the execution of their duties if they acted honestly and in good faith with a view to the best interests of the Company. &nbsp;Such limitations on liability may reduce the likelihood of litigation against the Company&#146;s officers and directors and may discourage or deter its shareholders from suing the Company&#146;s officers and directors based upon breaches of their duties to the Company, though such an action, if successful, might otherwise benefit the Company and its shareholders.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Key management employees may fail to properly carry out their duties or may leave which could negatively impact corporate operations and/or stock pricing.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>While developing, manufacturing, and marketing proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire, the nature of the Company&#146;s business, its ability to develop a successful sales force, and to develop a competitive edge in the marketplace, depends, in large part, on its ability to attract and maintain qualified key management personnel. &nbsp;Competition for such personnel is intense and the Company may not be able to attract and retain such personnel. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s growth will depend on the efforts of its Directors (David Corcoran, Michael Huddy, Victor Yates and Craig Roberts) and its Senior Management (President/CEO/Director, Michael Huddy; and CFO/Director, David Corcoran; and Corporate Secretary, Lindsey Nauen). &nbsp;David Corcoran and Lindsey Nauen work for the Company on a part-time basis while Michael Huddy works for the Company on a full-time basis. &nbsp;&nbsp;The Company has no key-man life insurance and there are no written agreements with them.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-19.2px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Operational Risks</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier&#146;s business is based on the premise that building projects occasionally require fire resistive performance. &nbsp;Whether based on a requirement of a national or local building code, the possibility for lower insurance rates, or simply the desire for safety by a building owner, Barrier&#146;s health as a manufacturing company is based on a demand for resistive building products. &nbsp;Any factor that could mitigate the demand for fire resistive construction could have a negative impact on Barrier.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier suffers a larger risk in the possibility that a new generation of technology that will impart fire resistance to building products may be developed. &nbsp;New technology may serve to decrease the demand for Barrier&#146;s Pyrotite&#174; products if the new technology proved to impart either better characteristics of fire performance or was found to be less expensive to produce and market than Blazeguard. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s management team makes a concerted effort to stay abreast of new technologies as they are being developed. &nbsp;Barrier does this by staying in close contact with the industry via trade associations (e.g. The National Association of Home Builders, NAHB) and the independent research laboratories that are asked to test these new technologies and products as they are developed. &nbsp;However, there is no guarantee that the Company is able to adopt and utilize the new technology. &nbsp;New technologies require years of testing, not only in development but in use, before they are accepted and &#147;evaluated for use&#148; by the major building code agencies such as The International Code Council (ICC).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>10</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier&#146;s business is directly related to housing/building starts in the United States. &nbsp;Any factor resulting in a slowdown of economic activity, especially those that result in an increase in interest rates will have a negative impact on Barrier&#146;s business. &nbsp;New housing starts in the U.S. are slowly starting to recover. &nbsp;The U.S. Census Bureau reported 750,000 new housing starts in August 2012 (adjusted on an annual basis). August's numbers were 2.3 percent higher than the July 2012 estimate of 733,000 and 29.1 percent higher than the August 2011 annually adjusted rate of 581,000. &nbsp;There continues to be a risk that the economy is not yet stable enough to support long term improvements in new housing starts. &nbsp;If housing growth is unstable, sales of Pyrotite&#174; products could be negatively impacted or unpredictable. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier presumes that corporate growth will be funded from positive cash flow, conventional bank loans, and from the occasional sale of equity to generate needed capital. &nbsp;The business plan, however, anticipates a few years of very rapid sales volume increases. &nbsp;Companies experiencing rapid growth depend upon solid support both in the market place and in the manufacturing facilities themselves. &nbsp;Ensuring that capital is available to increase production capacity and to provide support materials and training in the market place is essential to success.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier is relatively &#147;thin&#148; in its management and sales team. &nbsp;As a &#147;start-up&#148; company, Barrier has intentionally kept the number of middle and upper management and sales people at a minimum in an effort to conserve financial resources. &nbsp;As the company grows it will be essential to have new talent emerging to help provide leadership in the factories of production and in the market place to introduce the products to new markets: &nbsp;both in geography and in use. &nbsp;As long as the management/sales team is thin, the impact of losing a key player is very large.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Barrier relies on key relationships with industry leaders to maintain its position in the market place. &nbsp;Barrier is dependent upon suppliers to provide key elements of production at critical times at reasonable prices. &nbsp;While the majority of these materials are readily available and abundant, without quality suppliers providing reasonable terms of sales, Barrier would not be able to stay in business: there would be no operating or working goods of production to use in the manufacturing process.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-19.2px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=center><B>Risks Relating to the Company&#146;s Common Stock</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Principal stockholders, officers and directors have substantial control regarding stock ownership; this concentration could lead to conflicts of interest and difficulties in the &#147;public&#148; investors effecting corporate changes, and could adversely affect the Company&#146;s stock prices.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s Senior Management, Directors and greater-than-five-percent stockholders (and their affiliates), acting together, hold approximately 25.4% of the shares of the Company, on a diluted basis, and have the ability to control substantially all matters submitted to the Company&#146;s stockholders for approval (including the election and removal of directors and any merger, consolidation or sale of all or substantially all of the Company&#146;s assets) and to control the Company&#146;s management and affairs. &nbsp;Accordingly, this concentration of ownership may have the effect of delaying, deferring or preventing a change in control of the Company, impeding a merger, consolidation, takeover or other business combination involving the Company or discouraging a potential acquirer from making a tender offer or otherwise attempting to obtain control of the Company, which in turn could materially adversely affect the market price of the Company&#146;s stock.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Employee/Director/Consultant stock options could lead to greater concentration of stock ownership among insiders and could lead to dilution of stock ownership which could lead to depressed stock prices.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Because the success of the Company is highly dependent upon its respective employees, the Company has granted to some or all of its key employees, Directors and consultants options to purchase common shares as non-cash incentives. &nbsp;To the extent that significant numbers of such options may be granted and exercised, the interests of the other stockholders of the Company may be diluted causing possible loss of investment value.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>11</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>The Company has never declared or paid cash dividends on its common shares and does not anticipate doing so in the foreseeable future.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>There can be no assurance that the Company&#146;s Board of Directors will ever declare cash dividends, which action is exclusively within its discretion. &nbsp;Investors cannot expect to receive a dividend on the Company&#146;s common shares in the foreseeable future, if at all.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Low stock market prices and volume volatility for the Company&#146;s common shares create a risk that investors might not be able to effect purchases/sales at prices that accurately reflect corporate value.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The market for the common shares of the Company on the OTC Bulletin Board in the United States may be highly volatile for reasons both related to the performance of the Company or events pertaining to the industry (i.e., price fluctuation/technological change/new competitor) as well as factors unrelated to the Company or its industry. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s common shares can be expected to be subject to volatility in both price and volume arising from market expectations. &nbsp;Stockholders of the Company may be unable to sell significant quantities of common shares in the public trading markets without a significant reduction in the price of the common shares.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>Broker-Dealers may be discouraged from effecting transactions in the Company&#146;s common shares because they are subject to the penny stock rules.</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Rules 15g-1 through 15g-9 promulgated under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, impose sales practice and disclosure requirements on NASD broker-dealers who make a market in &#147;penny stock&#148;. &nbsp;A penny stock generally includes any non-NASDAQ equity security that has a market price of less than $5.00 per share. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s shares are quoted on the OTC Bulletin Board in the United States and the TSX Venture Exchange in Canada. &nbsp;The additional sales practice and disclosure requirements imposed upon broker-dealers may discourage broker-dealers from effecting transactions in the Company&#146;s shares, which could severely limit the market liquidity of the shares and impede the sale of the Company&#146;s shares in the secondary market.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Under the penny stock regulations, a broker-dealer selling penny stock to anyone other than an established customer or &#147;accredited investor&#148; (generally, an individual with net worth in excess of $1,000,000 or an annual income exceeding $200,000, or $300,000 together with his or her spouse) must make a special suitability determination for the purchaser and must receive the purchaser's written consent to the transaction prior to sale, unless the broker-dealer or the transaction is otherwise exempt.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>In addition, the penny stock regulations require the broker-dealer to deliver, prior to any transaction involving a penny stock, a disclosure schedule prepared by the US SEC relating to the penny stock market, unless the broker-dealer or the transaction is otherwise exempt. &nbsp;A broker-dealer is also required to disclose commissions payable to the broker-dealer and the registered representative and current quotations for the securities. &nbsp;Finally, a broker-dealer is required to send monthly statements disclosing recent price information with respect to the penny stock held in a customer's account and information with respect to the limited market in penny stocks.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<A NAME="_Toc305669986"></A><P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 1B. &nbsp;UNRESOLVED STAFF COMMENTS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman">None</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<A NAME="_Toc305669987"></A><P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 2. &nbsp;DESCRIPTION OF PROPERTY</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s operating and manufacturing facilities, along with executive offices, are located in leased premises at 510 Fourth Street North, Watkins, Minnesota. &nbsp;The Company entered into a 20-year &#147;capital lease&#148; beginning 6/1/1995. &nbsp;The lease allows the Company to purchase the facility for a small &#147;transfer fee&#148; once the 20-year lease is up and the industrial development bonds the City of Watkins issued to fund the project are paid in full.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>12</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-bottom:9.6px; padding-top:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s manufacturing complex consists of two manufacturing lines housed in the main building. &nbsp;A 2,500 square-foot office is located in the front of this building. &nbsp;To the immediate east of the main drive, a storage building (40&#146; x 60&#146;) allows for short-term storage of untreated sheathing.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The earlier of the two production lines, our spray technology line, is housed nearest the offices and occupies approximately 22,000 sq. ft. of space. &nbsp;This line is primarily used for panels larger than 4&#146; x 8&#146; or for production not suited for the highly automated standard production line, including plywood. &nbsp;The mix for this line is produced in batches and fed through a reciprocating spray apparatus on to the panels. &nbsp;The fiberglass is supplied as roving and automatically chopped as it is applied to the panels. &nbsp;An infra-red oven supplies the energy to accelerate the cure of the coating; space is provided for the panels to be stacked. &nbsp;Specialty panels can be stacked in custom designed racks if required. The designed capacity from this line is 10MM board feet per shift.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The newer of the two lines, our automated line, is housed in the extension added to the main building in 2004. &nbsp;This portion of the building is 15,000 sq. feet and houses a completely separate line. &nbsp;This line runs at 20 feet per minute and is capable of producing over 20MM board feet per shift annually when running at 100% efficiency. &nbsp;We currently need to operate this line one shift only, but could quickly increase our capacity to meet market demand by adding shift(s). &nbsp;Automation efficiencies on this line cover: unstacking and restacking of panels; use of automated Pyrotite coating equipment, a computer controlled mixing area; automatic panel weight information fed back continuously to the operators; and a custom panel curing system. &nbsp;This line produces panels of much higher, consistent quality than the older line, at a much more marketable cost point.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Future growth plans may include plants modeled after this new line, placed strategically near markets of prime opportunity; built either by Barrier or with licensed partners.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>Regardless of which line is used, the production process for the Pyrotite technology contains no hazardous or controlled substances that could raise environmental concerns. &nbsp;&nbsp;The majority of materials used in the production of Pyrotite are naturally occurring and are therefore accepted at local land-fills. &nbsp;Use and handling instructions for the Company&#146;s finished products are no more stringent than those required for handling other natural wood based building products.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<A NAME="_Toc305669988"></A><P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 3. &nbsp;LEGAL PROCEEDINGS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Directors and the management of the Company know of no other material, active or pending, legal proceedings against them; nor is the Company involved as a plaintiff in any material proceeding or pending litigation.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Directors and the management of the Company know of no active or pending proceedings against anyone that might materially adversely affect an interest of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Dividends</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman" align=justify>The Company has not declared any dividends since incorporation and does not anticipate that it will do so in the foreseeable future. &nbsp;The present policy of the Company is to retain future earnings for use in its operations and expansion of its business. &nbsp;There are no restrictions that limit the ability of the Company to pay dividends on common equity or that are likely to do so in the future.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Use of Proceeds From Sales of Securities is for working capital</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman"><B><U>Recent Sales of Unregistered Securities</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman">The Company relied on the exemptions from registration under Regulation S for the following private placements of securities to only Canadian residents:</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-38.4px; text-indent:19.2px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman">Fiscal 2010: 15,000,000 units at CDN$0.10 per unit = US$1,482,974 (CDN$1,500,000)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:19.2px; font-family:Courier New,Times New Roman">Fiscal 2011: 40,000 units at US$0.09 per unit = US$3,600</P>
